				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For the 2000 TV film, see <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_(2000_film)" title="Nuremberg (2000 film)">Nuremberg (2000 film)</a>. <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Nürnberg" redirects here.  It is not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/N%C3%BCrburg" title="Nürburg">Nürburg</a>. For ships named "Nürnberg", see <a href="/wiki/SMS_N%C3%BCrnberg" title="SMS Nürnberg">SMS Nürnberg</a>.</div>

<p><b>Nuremberg</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/nj/: 'n' in 'new'">nj</span><span title="/ʊər/: 'our' in 'tour'">ʊər</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/ɜːr/: 'ur' in 'fur'">ɜːr</span><span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span></span>/</a></span></span>; German: <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><i>Nürnberg</i></span>; <small>pronounced</small> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German" title="Help:IPA/Standard German">[ˈnʏɐ̯nbɛɐ̯k]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:N%C3%BCrnberg.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a8/N%C3%BCrnberg.ogg" class="internal" title="Nürnberg.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup>) is a city on the river <a href="/wiki/Pegnitz_(river)" title="Pegnitz (river)">Pegnitz</a> and on the <a href="/wiki/Rhine%E2%80%93Main%E2%80%93Danube_Canal" title="Rhine–Main–Danube Canal">Rhine–Main–Danube Canal</a> in the German <a href="/wiki/Bundesland_(Germany)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bundesland (Germany)">state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavaria</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Regierungsbezirk" title="Regierungsbezirk">administrative region</a> of <a href="/wiki/Middle_Franconia" title="Middle Franconia">Middle Franconia</a>, about 170 kilometres (110&#160;mi) north of <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>. It is the second-largest city in Bavaria (after Munich), and the largest in <a href="/wiki/Franconia" title="Franconia">Franconia</a> (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><i>Franken</i></span>). As of February 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> it had a population of 517,498, making it <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>'s fourteenth-largest city. The <a href="/wiki/Urban_area" title="Urban area">urban area</a> also includes <a href="/wiki/F%C3%BCrth" title="Fürth">Fürth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erlangen" title="Erlangen">Erlangen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Schwabach" title="Schwabach">Schwabach</a>, with a total population of 763,854. As of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the "European Metropolitan Area Nuremberg" had approximately 3.5 million inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-Nde_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nde-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Nuremberg" title="Timeline of Nuremberg">Timeline of Nuremberg</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Burgraviate_of_Nuremberg" title="Burgraviate of Nuremberg">Burgraviate of Nuremberg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Imperial_City_of_Nuremberg" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial City of Nuremberg">Imperial City of Nuremberg</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nuremberg_defensive_wall_north_f_burggarten_bastion_f_w.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Nuremberg_defensive_wall_north_f_burggarten_bastion_f_w.jpg/220px-Nuremberg_defensive_wall_north_f_burggarten_bastion_f_w.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Nuremberg_defensive_wall_north_f_burggarten_bastion_f_w.jpg/330px-Nuremberg_defensive_wall_north_f_burggarten_bastion_f_w.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Nuremberg_defensive_wall_north_f_burggarten_bastion_f_w.jpg/440px-Nuremberg_defensive_wall_north_f_burggarten_bastion_f_w.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nuremberg_defensive_wall_north_f_burggarten_bastion_f_w.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Old fortifications of Nuremberg</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><span class="nowrap">Nuremberg was</span>, according to the first documentary mention of the city in 1050, the location of an <a href="/wiki/Imperial_castle" title="Imperial castle">Imperial castle</a> between the <a href="/wiki/East_Franks" class="mw-redirect" title="East Franks">East Franks</a> and the Bavarian <a href="/wiki/March_of_the_Nordgau" title="March of the Nordgau">March of the Nordgau</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HLB:N.C3.BCrnberg_Entwicklung_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HLB:N.C3.BCrnberg_Entwicklung-4">[4]</a></sup> From 1050 to 1571, the city expanded and rose dramatically in importance due to its location on key trade routes. <a href="/wiki/Conrad_III_of_Germany" title="Conrad III of Germany">King Conrad III</a> established a <a href="/wiki/Burgraviate_of_Nuremberg" title="Burgraviate of Nuremberg">burgraviate</a>, with the first burgraves coming from the Austrian House of <a href="/wiki/Raabs_an_der_Thaya" title="Raabs an der Thaya">Raab</a> but, with the extinction of their male line around 1190, the burgraviate was inherited by the last count's son-in-law, of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Hohenzollern" title="House of Hohenzollern">House of Hohenzollern</a>. From the late 12th century to the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire#Interregnum" title="Holy Roman Empire">Interregnum</a> (1254–73), however, the power of the burgraves diminished as the <a href="/wiki/Hohenstaufen" title="Hohenstaufen">Hohenstaufen</a> emperors transferred most non-military powers to a castellan, with the city administration and the municipal courts handed over to an Imperial mayor (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><i><a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reichsschulthei%C3%9F_(N%C3%BCrnberg)" class="extiw" title="de:Reichsschultheiß (Nürnberg)">Reichsschultheiß</a></i></span>) from 1173/74.<sup id="cite_ref-HLB:N.C3.BCrnberg_Entwicklung_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HLB:N.C3.BCrnberg_Entwicklung-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cath:Nuremberg_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cath:Nuremberg-5">[5]</a></sup> The strained relations between the burgraves and the castellan, with gradual transferral of powers to the latter in the late 14th and early 15th centuries, finally broke out into open enmity, which greatly influenced the history of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-Cath:Nuremberg_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cath:Nuremberg-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nuernberg_Burg_Panorama_PtGUI.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Nuernberg_Burg_Panorama_PtGUI.jpg/220px-Nuernberg_Burg_Panorama_PtGUI.jpg" width="220" height="107" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Nuernberg_Burg_Panorama_PtGUI.jpg/330px-Nuernberg_Burg_Panorama_PtGUI.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Nuernberg_Burg_Panorama_PtGUI.jpg/440px-Nuernberg_Burg_Panorama_PtGUI.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2889" data-file-height="1400" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nuernberg_Burg_Panorama_PtGUI.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Imperial Castle</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Nuremberg is often referred to as having been the 'unofficial capital' of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>, particularly because <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Diet_(Holy_Roman_Empire)" title="Imperial Diet (Holy Roman Empire)">Imperial Diet</a> (<i>Reichstag</i>) and courts met at <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Castle" title="Nuremberg Castle">Nuremberg Castle</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Diet_of_Nuremberg" title="Diet of Nuremberg">Diets of Nuremberg</a> were an important part of the administrative structure of the empire. The increasing demand of the royal court and the increasing importance of the city attracted increased trade and commerce to Nuremberg. In 1219, <a href="/wiki/Frederick_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Frederick II, Holy Roman Emperor">Frederick II</a> granted the <i><span lang="de" xml:lang="de">Großen Freiheitsbrief</span></i> (<i>Great Letter of Freedom</i>), including <a href="/wiki/German_town_law" title="German town law">town rights</a>, <a href="/wiki/Imperial_immediacy" title="Imperial immediacy">Imperial immediacy</a> (<i>Reichsfreiheit</i>), the privilege to mint coins, and an independent customs policy, almost wholly removing the city from the purview of the burgraves.<sup id="cite_ref-HLB:N.C3.BCrnberg_Entwicklung_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HLB:N.C3.BCrnberg_Entwicklung-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cath:Nuremberg_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cath:Nuremberg-5">[5]</a></sup> Nuremberg soon became, with <a href="/wiki/Augsburg" title="Augsburg">Augsburg</a>, one of the two great trade centers on the route from <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> to Northern Europe.</p>
<p>In 1298, the Jews of the town were accused of having <a href="/wiki/Host_desecration" title="Host desecration">desecrated</a> the <a href="/wiki/Sacramental_bread" title="Sacramental bread">host</a>, and 698 of them were killed in one of the many <a href="/wiki/Rintfleisch-Pogrom" class="mw-redirect" title="Rintfleisch-Pogrom">Rintfleisch Massacres</a>. Behind the massacre of 1298 was also the desire to combine the northern and southern parts of the city, which were divided by the <a href="/wiki/Pegnitz_(river)" title="Pegnitz (river)">Pegnitz</a>. The Jews of the German lands suffered many massacres during the <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">plague</a> years. In 1349, Nuremberg's Jews were subjected to a pogrom.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> They were burned at the stake or expelled, and a marketplace was built over the former Jewish quarter.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>The plague returned to the city in 1405, 1435, 1437, 1482, 1494, 1520 and 1534.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nuremberg_chronicles_-_Nuremberga.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Nuremberg_chronicles_-_Nuremberga.png/220px-Nuremberg_chronicles_-_Nuremberga.png" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Nuremberg_chronicles_-_Nuremberga.png/330px-Nuremberg_chronicles_-_Nuremberga.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Nuremberg_chronicles_-_Nuremberga.png/440px-Nuremberg_chronicles_-_Nuremberga.png 2x" data-file-width="2064" data-file-height="1372" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nuremberg_chronicles_-_Nuremberga.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Nuremberg in 1493<br />
(from the <i><a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Chronicle" title="Nuremberg Chronicle">Nuremberg Chronicle</a></i>).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The largest gains for Nuremberg were in the 14th century; including <a href="/wiki/Charles_IV,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles IV, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles IV</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Golden_Bull_of_1356" title="Golden Bull of 1356">Golden Bull of 1356</a>, naming Nuremberg as the city where newly elected <a href="/wiki/Kings_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Kings of Germany">kings of Germany</a> must hold their first Imperial Diet, making Nuremberg one of the three most important cities of the Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-HLB:N.C3.BCrnberg_Entwicklung_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HLB:N.C3.BCrnberg_Entwicklung-4">[4]</a></sup> Charles was the patron of the <a href="/wiki/Frauenkirche,_Nuremberg" title="Frauenkirche, Nuremberg">Frauenkirche</a>, built between 1352 and 1362 (the architect was likely <a href="/wiki/Peter_Parler" title="Peter Parler">Peter Parler</a>), where the Imperial court worshipped during its stays in Nuremberg. The royal and Imperial connection was strengthened when <a href="/wiki/Sigismund,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Sigismund, Holy Roman Emperor">Sigismund of Luxembourg</a> granted the Imperial regalia to be kept permanently in Nuremberg in 1423, where they remained until 1796, when the advancing French troops required their removal to <a href="/wiki/Regensburg" title="Regensburg">Regensburg</a> and thence to <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HLB:N.C3.BCrnberg_Entwicklung_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HLB:N.C3.BCrnberg_Entwicklung-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1349 the members of the <a href="/wiki/Guild" title="Guild">guilds</a> unsuccessfully rebelled against the patricians in the <i>Handwerkeraufstand</i> (<i>Craftsmen's Uprising</i>), supported by merchants and some councillors, leading to a ban on any self-organisation of the artisans in the city, abolishing the guilds that were customary elsewhere in Europe; the unions were then dissolved, and the oligarchs remained in power while Nuremberg was a free city.<sup id="cite_ref-HLB:N.C3.BCrnberg_Entwicklung_4-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HLB:N.C3.BCrnberg_Entwicklung-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cath:Nuremberg_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cath:Nuremberg-5">[5]</a></sup> Charles IV conferred upon the city the right to conclude alliances independently, thereby placing it upon a politically equal footing with the princes of the empire.<sup id="cite_ref-Cath:Nuremberg_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cath:Nuremberg-5">[5]</a></sup> Frequent fights took place with the burgraves without, however, inflicting lasting damage upon the city. After the castle had been destroyed by fire in 1420 during a feud between <a href="/wiki/Frederick_I,_Elector_of_Brandenburg" title="Frederick I, Elector of Brandenburg">Frederick IV</a> (since 1417 <a href="/wiki/Margrave_of_Brandenburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Margrave of Brandenburg">margrave of Brandenburg</a>) and the duke of <a href="/wiki/Bavaria-Ingolstadt" title="Bavaria-Ingolstadt">Bavaria-Ingolstadt</a>, the ruins and the forest belonging to the castle were purchased by the city (1427), resulting in the city's total sovereignty within its borders. Through these and other acquisitions the city accumulated considerable territory.<sup id="cite_ref-Cath:Nuremberg_5-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cath:Nuremberg-5">[5]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Hussite_Wars" title="Hussite Wars">Hussite Wars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black_Death#Recurrence" title="Black Death">recurrence of the Black Death</a> in 1437, and the <a href="/wiki/First_Margrave_War" title="First Margrave War">First Margrave War</a> led to a severe fall in population in the mid-15th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Cath:Nuremberg_5-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cath:Nuremberg-5">[5]</a></sup> At the beginning of the 16th century, siding with <a href="/wiki/Albert_IV,_Duke_of_Bavaria" title="Albert IV, Duke of Bavaria">Albert IV</a>, Duke of <a href="/wiki/Bavaria-Munich" title="Bavaria-Munich">Bavaria-Munich</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Landshut_War_of_Succession" class="mw-redirect" title="Landshut War of Succession">Landshut War of Succession</a> led the city to gain substantial territory, resulting in lands of 25&#160;sq&#160;mi (64.7&#160;km<sup>2</sup>), becoming one of the largest Imperial cities.<sup id="cite_ref-Cath:Nuremberg_5-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cath:Nuremberg-5">[5]</a></sup> During the Middle Ages, Nuremberg's literary culture was rich, varied, and influential.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_modern_age">Early modern age</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early modern age">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:De_Merian_Frankoniae_090.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/De_Merian_Frankoniae_090.jpg/220px-De_Merian_Frankoniae_090.jpg" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/De_Merian_Frankoniae_090.jpg/330px-De_Merian_Frankoniae_090.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/De_Merian_Frankoniae_090.jpg/440px-De_Merian_Frankoniae_090.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4620" data-file-height="3504" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:De_Merian_Frankoniae_090.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of Nuremberg, 1648</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The cultural flowering of Nuremberg, in the 15th and 16th centuries, made it the centre of the <a href="/wiki/German_Renaissance" title="German Renaissance">German Renaissance</a>. In 1525, Nuremberg accepted the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant Reformation">Protestant Reformation</a>, and in 1532, the religious Peace of Nuremberg, by which the <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutherans</a> gained important concessions, was signed there.<sup id="cite_ref-Cath:Nuremberg_5-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cath:Nuremberg-5">[5]</a></sup> During the 1552 revolution against <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V</a>, Nuremberg tried to purchase its neutrality, but the city was attacked without a declaration of war and was forced into a disadvantageous peace.<sup id="cite_ref-Cath:Nuremberg_5-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cath:Nuremberg-5">[5]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Augsburg" title="Peace of Augsburg">Peace of Augsburg</a>, the possessions of the Protestants were confirmed by the Emperor, their religious privileges extended and their independence from the <a href="/wiki/Bishopric_of_Bamberg" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishopric of Bamberg">Bishop of Bamberg</a> affirmed, while the 1520s' secularisation of the monasteries was also approved.<sup id="cite_ref-Cath:Nuremberg_5-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cath:Nuremberg-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_town_hall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Old_town_hall.jpg/170px-Old_town_hall.jpg" width="170" height="256" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Old_town_hall.jpg/255px-Old_town_hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Old_town_hall.jpg/340px-Old_town_hall.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1327" data-file-height="1997" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_town_hall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Wolffscher Bau</i> of the old city hall</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The state of affairs in the early 16th century, increased trade routes elsewhere and the ossification of the social hierarchy and legal structures contributed to the decline in trade.<sup id="cite_ref-Cath:Nuremberg_5-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cath:Nuremberg-5">[5]</a></sup> Frequent quartering of Imperial, Swedish and <a href="/wiki/Catholic_League_(German)" title="Catholic League (German)">League</a> soldiers, the financial costs of the war and the cessation of trade caused irreparable damage to the city and a near-halving of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-Cath:Nuremberg_5-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cath:Nuremberg-5">[5]</a></sup> In 1632, the city, occupied by the forces of <a href="/wiki/Gustavus_Adolphus_of_Sweden" title="Gustavus Adolphus of Sweden">Gustavus Adolphus of Sweden</a>, was <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Nuremberg" title="Siege of Nuremberg">besieged</a> by the army of Imperial general <a href="/wiki/Albrecht_von_Wallenstein" title="Albrecht von Wallenstein">Albrecht von Wallenstein</a>. The city declined after the war and recovered its importance only in the 19th century, when it grew as an industrial centre. Even after the Thirty Years' War, however, there was a late flowering of architecture and culture – secular <a href="/wiki/Baroque_architecture" title="Baroque architecture">Baroque architecture</a> is exemplified in the layout of the civic gardens built outside the city walls, and in the Protestant city's rebuilding of the <a href="/wiki/St._Egidien,_Nuremberg" title="St. Egidien, Nuremberg">Egidienkirche</a>, destroyed by fire at the beginning of the 18th century, considered a significant contribution to the baroque church architecture of Middle Franconia.<sup id="cite_ref-HLB:N.C3.BCrnberg_Entwicklung_4-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HLB:N.C3.BCrnberg_Entwicklung-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the Thirty Years' War, Nuremberg attempted to remain detached from external affairs, but contributions were demanded for the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Austrian_Succession" title="War of the Austrian Succession">War of the Austrian Succession</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a> and restrictions of imports and exports deprived the city of many markets for its manufactures.<sup id="cite_ref-Cath:Nuremberg_5-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cath:Nuremberg-5">[5]</a></sup> The Bavarian elector, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Theodore,_Elector_of_Bavaria" title="Charles Theodore, Elector of Bavaria">Charles Theodore</a>, appropriated part of the land obtained by the city during the <a href="/wiki/Landshut_War_of_Succession" class="mw-redirect" title="Landshut War of Succession">Landshut War of Succession</a>, to which Bavaria had maintained its claim; Prussia also claimed part of the territory. Realising its weakness, the city asked to be incorporated into Prussia but <a href="/wiki/Frederick_William_II_of_Prussia" title="Frederick William II of Prussia">Frederick William II</a> refused, fearing to offend Austria, <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russia</a> and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Cath:Nuremberg_5-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cath:Nuremberg-5">[5]</a></sup> At the Imperial diet in 1803, the independence of Nuremberg was affirmed, but on the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_the_Rhine" title="Confederation of the Rhine">Confederation of the Rhine</a> on 12 July 1806, it was agreed to hand the city over to Bavaria from 8 September, with Bavaria guaranteeing the <a href="/wiki/Amortisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Amortisation">amortisation</a> of the city's 12.5 million guilder public debt.<sup id="cite_ref-Cath:Nuremberg_5-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cath:Nuremberg-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="After_the_Great_French_War">After the Great French War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: After the Great French War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bavaria" title="Kingdom of Bavaria">Kingdom of Bavaria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nuremberg_Scrapbooks_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Nuremberg_Scrapbooks_cropped.jpg/220px-Nuremberg_Scrapbooks_cropped.jpg" width="220" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Nuremberg_Scrapbooks_cropped.jpg/330px-Nuremberg_Scrapbooks_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Nuremberg_Scrapbooks_cropped.jpg/440px-Nuremberg_Scrapbooks_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1016" data-file-height="790" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nuremberg_Scrapbooks_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Old town of Nuremberg in the 19th century</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Adler_Originalfoto.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Adler_Originalfoto.jpg/220px-Adler_Originalfoto.jpg" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Adler_Originalfoto.jpg/330px-Adler_Originalfoto.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Adler_Originalfoto.jpg/440px-Adler_Originalfoto.jpg 2x" data-file-width="584" data-file-height="351" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Adler_Originalfoto.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The British-built <i><a href="/wiki/Adler_(locomotive)" title="Adler (locomotive)">Adler</a></i> was the locomotive of the first German Railway between Nuremberg and Fürth.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the fall of <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a>, the city's trade and commerce revived; the skill of its inhabitants together with its favourable situation soon made the city prosperous, particularly after its public debt had been acknowledged as a part of the Bavarian national debt. Having been incorporated into a Catholic country, the city was compelled to refrain from further discrimination against Catholics, who had been excluded from the rights of citizenship. Catholic services had been celebrated in the city by the priests of the <a href="/wiki/Teutonic_Order" title="Teutonic Order">Teutonic Order</a>, often under great difficulties. After their possessions had been confiscated by the Bavarian government in 1806, they were given the Frauenkirche on the Market in 1809; in 1810 the first Catholic parish was established, which in 1818 numbered 1,010 souls.<sup id="cite_ref-Cath:Nuremberg_5-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cath:Nuremberg-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1817, the city was incorporated into the district of <a href="/wiki/Rezatkreis" title="Rezatkreis">Rezatkreis</a> (named for the river <a href="/wiki/Fr%C3%A4nkische_Rezat" class="mw-redirect" title="Fränkische Rezat">Franconian Rezat</a>), which was renamed to <a href="/wiki/Middle_Franconia" title="Middle Franconia">Middle Franconia</a> (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><i><a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mittelfranken" class="extiw" title="de:Mittelfranken">Mittelfranken</a></i></span>) on 1 January 1838.<sup id="cite_ref-Cath:Nuremberg_5-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cath:Nuremberg-5">[5]</a></sup> The first German railway, the <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_Ludwigsbahn" class="mw-redirect" title="Bavarian Ludwigsbahn">Bavarian Ludwigsbahn</a>, from Nuremberg to nearby <a href="/wiki/F%C3%BCrth" title="Fürth">Fürth</a>, was opened in 1835. The establishment of railways and the incorporation of Bavaria into <a href="/wiki/Zollverein" title="Zollverein">Zollverein</a> (the 19th-century German Customs Union), commerce and industry opened the way to greater prosperity.<sup id="cite_ref-Cath:Nuremberg_5-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cath:Nuremberg-5">[5]</a></sup> In 1852, there were 53,638 inhabitants: 46,441 Protestants and 6,616 Catholics. It subsequently grew to become the most important industrial city of Bavaria and one of the most prosperous towns of southern Germany but after the Austrian prussian war it was given to prussia in governmental power in extange for part of the taxes from there<sup id="cite_ref-Cath:Nuremberg_5-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cath:Nuremberg-5">[5]</a></sup> In 1905, its population, including several incorporated suburbs, was 291,351: 86,943 Catholics, 196,913 Protestants, 3,738 Jews and 3,766 members of other creeds.<sup id="cite_ref-Cath:Nuremberg_5-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cath:Nuremberg-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nazi_era">Nazi era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Nazi era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Reichsparteitag_1935_Gro%C3%9Fer_Appell_28-1121M_original.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Reichsparteitag_1935_Gro%C3%9Fer_Appell_28-1121M_original.jpg/170px-Reichsparteitag_1935_Gro%C3%9Fer_Appell_28-1121M_original.jpg" width="170" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Reichsparteitag_1935_Gro%C3%9Fer_Appell_28-1121M_original.jpg/255px-Reichsparteitag_1935_Gro%C3%9Fer_Appell_28-1121M_original.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Reichsparteitag_1935_Gro%C3%9Fer_Appell_28-1121M_original.jpg/340px-Reichsparteitag_1935_Gro%C3%9Fer_Appell_28-1121M_original.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2346" data-file-height="2951" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Reichsparteitag_1935_Gro%C3%9Fer_Appell_28-1121M_original.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_rally" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuremberg rally">Nuremberg rally</a>, 1935</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Nuremberg held great significance during the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> era. Because of the city's relevance to the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> and its position in the centre of Germany, the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">Nazi Party</a> chose the city to be the site of huge Nazi Party conventions&#160;— the <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Rally" title="Nuremberg Rally">Nuremberg rallies</a>. The rallies were held 1927, 1929 and annually 1933–1938 in Nuremberg. After <a href="/wiki/Machtergreifung" class="mw-redirect" title="Machtergreifung">Adolf Hitler's rise to power</a> in 1933 the Nuremberg rallies became huge <a href="/wiki/Nazi_propaganda" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazi propaganda">Nazi propaganda</a> events, a centre of Nazi ideals. The 1934 rally was filmed by <a href="/wiki/Leni_Riefenstahl" title="Leni Riefenstahl">Leni Riefenstahl</a>, and made into a propaganda film called <i>Triumph des Willens</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Triumph_of_the_Will" title="Triumph of the Will">Triumph of the Will</a></i>). At the 1935 rally, Hitler specifically ordered the <a href="/wiki/Reichstag_(Weimar_Republic)" title="Reichstag (Weimar Republic)">Reichstag</a> to convene at Nuremberg to pass the anti-Semitic <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Laws" title="Nuremberg Laws">Nuremberg Laws</a> which revoked German <a href="/wiki/Citizenship" title="Citizenship">citizenship</a> for all Jews and other non-Aryans. A number of premises were constructed solely for these assemblies, some of which were not finished. Today many examples of <a href="/wiki/Nazi_architecture" title="Nazi architecture">Nazi architecture</a> can still be seen in the city. The city was also the home of the Nazi <a href="/wiki/Propaganda" title="Propaganda">propagandist</a> <a href="/wiki/Julius_Streicher" title="Julius Streicher">Julius Streicher</a>, the publisher of <i><a href="/wiki/Der_St%C3%BCrmer" title="Der Stürmer">Der Stürmer</a></i>.</p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:288px;max-width:288px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:142px;max-width:142px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:1945.02.12._Plan_der_Zerst%C3%B6rungen_N%C3%BCrnbergs.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/1945.02.12._Plan_der_Zerst%C3%B6rungen_N%C3%BCrnbergs.jpg/140px-1945.02.12._Plan_der_Zerst%C3%B6rungen_N%C3%BCrnbergs.jpg" width="140" height="122" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/1945.02.12._Plan_der_Zerst%C3%B6rungen_N%C3%BCrnbergs.jpg/210px-1945.02.12._Plan_der_Zerst%C3%B6rungen_N%C3%BCrnbergs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/1945.02.12._Plan_der_Zerst%C3%B6rungen_N%C3%BCrnbergs.jpg/280px-1945.02.12._Plan_der_Zerst%C3%B6rungen_N%C3%BCrnbergs.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4081" data-file-height="3561" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Map of city centre with air raid destruction</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:142px;max-width:142px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Nuremberg_in_Ruins_1945_HD-SN-99-02986.JPEG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Nuremberg_in_Ruins_1945_HD-SN-99-02986.JPEG/140px-Nuremberg_in_Ruins_1945_HD-SN-99-02986.JPEG" width="140" height="193" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Nuremberg_in_Ruins_1945_HD-SN-99-02986.JPEG/210px-Nuremberg_in_Ruins_1945_HD-SN-99-02986.JPEG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Nuremberg_in_Ruins_1945_HD-SN-99-02986.JPEG/280px-Nuremberg_in_Ruins_1945_HD-SN-99-02986.JPEG 2x" data-file-width="2176" data-file-height="3000" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The bombed-out city of Nuremberg, 1945</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, Nuremberg was the headquarters of <i><a href="/wiki/Wehrkreis" class="mw-redirect" title="Wehrkreis">Wehrkreis</a></i> (military district) XIII, and an important site for military production, including aircraft, submarines and tank engines. A subcamp of <a href="/wiki/Flossenb%C3%BCrg_concentration_camp" title="Flossenbürg concentration camp">Flossenbürg concentration camp</a> was located here. Extensive use was made of <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slave labour</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> The city was severely damaged in <a href="/wiki/Strategic_bombing_during_World_War_II" title="Strategic bombing during World War II">Allied strategic bombing</a> from 1943 to 1945. On 29 March 1944, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">RAF</a> endured its heaviest losses in the bombing campaign of Germany. Out of more than 700 planes participating, 106 were shot down or crash landed on the way home to their base, and more than 700 men were missing, as many as 545 of them dead. More than 160 became prisoners of war.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> On 2 January 1945, the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">medieval</a> city centre was systematically bombed by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Air_Forces" title="United States Army Air Forces">U.S. Army Air Forces</a> and about ninety percent of it was destroyed in only one hour, with 1,800 residents killed and roughly 100,000 displaced. In February 1945, additional attacks followed. In total, about 6,000 Nuremberg residents are estimated to have been killed in air raids.</p>
<p>Nuremberg was a heavily fortified city that was captured in <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Nuremberg_(1945)" title="Battle of Nuremberg (1945)">a fierce battle</a> lasting from 17 to 21 April 1945 by the U.S. <a href="/wiki/3rd_Infantry_Division_(United_States)" title="3rd Infantry Division (United States)">3rd Infantry Division</a>, <a href="/wiki/42nd_Infantry_Division_(United_States)" title="42nd Infantry Division (United States)">42nd Infantry Division</a> and <a href="/wiki/45th_Infantry_Division_(United_States)" title="45th Infantry Division (United States)">45th Infantry Division</a>, which fought house-to-house and street-by-street against determined German resistance, causing further urban devastation to the already bombed and shelled buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Despite this intense degree of destruction, the city was rebuilt after the war and was to some extent, restored to its pre-war appearance including the reconstruction of some of its medieval buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> However, over half of the historic look of the center, and especially the northeastern half of the old <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Free_City" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial Free City">Imperial Free City</a> was lost forever.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nuremberg_trials">Nuremberg trials</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Nuremberg trials">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_trials" title="Nuremberg trials">Nuremberg trials</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Defendants_in_the_dock_at_nuremberg_trials.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Defendants_in_the_dock_at_nuremberg_trials.jpg/220px-Defendants_in_the_dock_at_nuremberg_trials.jpg" width="220" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Defendants_in_the_dock_at_nuremberg_trials.jpg/330px-Defendants_in_the_dock_at_nuremberg_trials.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Defendants_in_the_dock_at_nuremberg_trials.jpg/440px-Defendants_in_the_dock_at_nuremberg_trials.jpg 2x" data-file-width="761" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Defendants_in_the_dock_at_nuremberg_trials.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Defendants in the dock at the Nuremberg trials</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Between 1945 and 1946, German officials involved in war crimes and crimes against humanity were brought before an international tribunal in the Nuremberg trials. The <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> had wanted these trials to take place in <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>. However, Nuremberg was chosen as the site for the trials for specific reasons:</p>
<ul>
<li>The city had been the location of the Nazi Party's Nuremberg rallies and the laws stripping Jews of their citizenship were passed there. There was symbolic value in making it the place of Nazi demise.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Justice,_Nuremberg" title="Palace of Justice, Nuremberg">Palace of Justice</a> was spacious and largely undamaged (one of the few that had remained largely intact despite extensive Allied bombing of Germany). The already large courtroom was reasonably easily expanded by the removal of the wall at the end opposite the bench, thereby incorporating the adjoining room. A large prison was also part of the complex.</li>
<li>As a compromise, it was agreed that Berlin would become the permanent seat of the International Military Tribunal and that the first trial (several were planned) would take place in Nuremberg. Due to the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, subsequent trials never took place.</li>
</ul>
<p>The same courtroom in Nuremberg was the venue of the <a href="/wiki/Subsequent_Nuremberg_Trials" class="mw-redirect" title="Subsequent Nuremberg Trials">Nuremberg Military Tribunals</a>, organized by the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> as <a href="/wiki/Allied-occupied_Germany" title="Allied-occupied Germany">occupying power</a> in the area.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_climate">Geography and climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geography and climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nuremberg_Map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Nuremberg_Map.png/220px-Nuremberg_Map.png" width="220" height="218" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Nuremberg_Map.png/330px-Nuremberg_Map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Nuremberg_Map.png/440px-Nuremberg_Map.png 2x" data-file-width="1702" data-file-height="1683" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nuremberg_Map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of Nuremberg</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Several old villages now belong to the city, for example <a href="/w/index.php?title=Grossgr%C3%BCndlach&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Grossgründlach (page does not exist)">Grossgründlach</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kraftshof&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kraftshof (page does not exist)">Kraftshof</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Thon_(Nuremberg)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Thon (Nuremberg) (page does not exist)">Thon</a>, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Neunhof&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Neunhof (page does not exist)">Neunhof</a> in the north-west; <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ziegelstein&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ziegelstein (page does not exist)">Ziegelstein</a> in the north-east, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Altenfurt&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Altenfurt (page does not exist)">Altenfurt</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Fischbach_bei_N%C3%BCrnberg&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Fischbach bei Nürnberg (page does not exist)">Fischbach</a> in the south-east; and <a href="/wiki/Katzwang" title="Katzwang">Katzwang</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kornburg&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kornburg (page does not exist)">Kornburg</a> in the south. <a href="/wiki/Langwasser" title="Langwasser">Langwasser</a> is a modern suburb.</p>
<p>Nuremberg has an <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a> (Koppen: Cfb), influenced by its inland position and higher altitude causing seasonal differences reminiscent of continental climates, although its winters are somewhat milder. Winters are diverse, with either mild or cold weather: the average temperature is around −3&#160;°C (27&#160;°F) to 4&#160;°C (39&#160;°F), while summers are generally warm, mostly around 13&#160;°C (55&#160;°F) at night to 25&#160;°C (77&#160;°F) in the afternoon. Precipitation is evenly spread throughout the year, although February and April tend to be a bit drier whereas July tends to have more rainfall.</p>

<p>Nuremberg has been a popular destination for immigrants. 39.5&#160;% of the residents had an immigrant background in 2010 (counted with MigraPro).<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(July 2011)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Nuremberg for many people is still associated with its traditional gingerbread (<i><a href="/wiki/Lebkuchen" title="Lebkuchen">Lebkuchen</a></i>) products, sausages, and handmade toys. <a href="/wiki/Pocket_watch" title="Pocket watch">Pocket watches</a> — <i><a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_eggs" title="Nuremberg eggs">Nuremberg eggs</a></i> — were made here in the 16th century by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Henlein" title="Peter Henlein">Peter Henlein</a>. In the 19th century Nuremberg became the "industrial heart" of <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavaria</a> with companies such as <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a> and <a href="/wiki/MAN_SE" title="MAN SE">MAN</a> establishing a strong base in the city. Nuremberg is still an important industrial centre with a strong standing in the markets of Central and Eastern Europe. Items manufactured in the area include electrical equipment, mechanical and optical products, motor vehicles, writing and drawing paraphernalia, stationery products, and printed materials. The city is also strong in the fields of automation, energy, and medical technology. Siemens is still the largest industrial employer in the Nuremberg region but a good third of German market research agencies are also located in the city. The <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_International_Toy_Fair" title="Nuremberg International Toy Fair">Nuremberg International Toy Fair</a> is the largest of its kind in the world. The city also hosts several specialist hi-tech fairs every year, attracting experts from every corner of the globe.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Durerhaus-nbg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Durerhaus-nbg.jpg/170px-Durerhaus-nbg.jpg" width="170" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Durerhaus-nbg.jpg/255px-Durerhaus-nbg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Durerhaus-nbg.jpg/340px-Durerhaus-nbg.jpg 2x" data-file-width="379" data-file-height="531" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Durerhaus-nbg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Albrecht_D%C3%BCrer%27s_House" title="Albrecht Dürer's House">Albrecht Dürer's House</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Christkindlesmarkt_nuernberg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Christkindlesmarkt_nuernberg.jpg/170px-Christkindlesmarkt_nuernberg.jpg" width="170" height="229" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Christkindlesmarkt_nuernberg.jpg/255px-Christkindlesmarkt_nuernberg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Christkindlesmarkt_nuernberg.jpg/340px-Christkindlesmarkt_nuernberg.jpg 2x" data-file-width="627" data-file-height="843" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Christkindlesmarkt_nuernberg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Christkindlesmarkt,_Nuremberg" title="Christkindlesmarkt, Nuremberg">Christkindlesmarkt</a> with <i>Schöner Brunnen</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Nuremberg was an early centre of humanism, science, printing, and mechanical invention. The city contributed much to the science of <a href="/wiki/Astronomy" title="Astronomy">astronomy</a>. In 1471 Johannes Mueller of <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6nigsberg,_Bavaria" title="Königsberg, Bavaria">Königsberg</a> (Bavaria), later called <a href="/wiki/Regiomontanus" title="Regiomontanus">Regiomontanus</a>, built an astronomical observatory in Nuremberg and published many important astronomical charts. In 1515, <a href="/wiki/Albrecht_D%C3%BCrer" title="Albrecht Dürer">Albrecht Dürer</a>, a native of Nuremberg, created woodcuts of the first maps of the stars of the northern and southern hemispheres, producing the first printed star charts, which had been ordered by <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Stabius" title="Johannes Stabius">Johannes Stabius</a>. Around 1515 Dürer also published the "Stabiussche Weltkarte", the first perspective drawing of the terrestrial globe. Perhaps most famously, the main part of <a href="/wiki/Nicolaus_Copernicus" title="Nicolaus Copernicus">Nicolaus Copernicus</a>'s work was published in Nuremberg in 1543.</p>
<p>Printers and publishers have a long history in Nuremberg. Many of these publishers worked with well-known artists of the day to produce books that could also be considered works of art. In 1470 <a href="/wiki/Anton_Koberger" title="Anton Koberger">Anton Koberger</a> opened Europe's first print shop in Nuremberg. In 1493, he published the <i>Nuremberg Chronicles</i>, also known as the <i>World Chronicles</i> (<i>Schedelsche Weltchronik</i>), an illustrated history of the world from the creation to the present day. It was written in the local Franconian dialect by <a href="/wiki/Hartmann_Schedel" title="Hartmann Schedel">Hartmann Schedel</a> and had illustrations by <a href="/wiki/Michael_Wolgemut" title="Michael Wolgemut">Michael Wohlgemuth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hans_Pleydenwurff" title="Hans Pleydenwurff">Wilhelm Pleydenwurff</a>, and Albrecht Dürer. Others furthered geographical knowledge and travel by map making. Notable among these was navigator and geographer <a href="/wiki/Martin_Behaim" title="Martin Behaim">Martin Behaim</a>, who made the first world globe.</p>
<p>Sculptors such as <a href="/wiki/Veit_Stoss" title="Veit Stoss">Veit Stoss</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adam_Kraft" title="Adam Kraft">Adam Kraft</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peter_Vischer_the_Elder" title="Peter Vischer the Elder">Peter Vischer</a> are also associated with Nuremberg.</p>
<p>Composed of prosperous artisans, the guilds of the <a href="/wiki/Meistersinger" title="Meistersinger">Meistersingers</a> flourished here. <a href="/wiki/Richard_Wagner" title="Richard Wagner">Richard Wagner</a> made their most famous member, <a href="/wiki/Hans_Sachs" title="Hans Sachs">Hans Sachs</a>, the hero of his opera <i><a href="/wiki/Die_Meistersinger_von_N%C3%BCrnberg" title="Die Meistersinger von Nürnberg">Die Meistersinger von Nürnberg</a></i>. Baroque composer <a href="/wiki/Johann_Pachelbel" title="Johann Pachelbel">Johann Pachelbel</a> was born here and was organist of <a href="/wiki/St._Sebaldus_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Sebaldus Church">St. Sebaldus Church</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Fine_Arts,_Nuremberg" title="Academy of Fine Arts, Nuremberg">academy of fine arts</a> situated in Nuremberg is the oldest art academy in central Europe and looks back to a tradition of 350 years of artistic education.</p>
<p>Nuremberg is also famous for its <a href="/wiki/Christkindlesmarkt,_Nuremberg" title="Christkindlesmarkt, Nuremberg">Christkindlesmarkt</a> (Christmas market), which draws well over a million shoppers each year. The market is famous for its handmade ornaments and delicacies.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Performing_arts">Performing arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Performing arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Staatstheater_N%C3%BCrnberg_2006-08-08.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Staatstheater_N%C3%BCrnberg_2006-08-08.jpg/220px-Staatstheater_N%C3%BCrnberg_2006-08-08.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Staatstheater_N%C3%BCrnberg_2006-08-08.jpg/330px-Staatstheater_N%C3%BCrnberg_2006-08-08.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Staatstheater_N%C3%BCrnberg_2006-08-08.jpg/440px-Staatstheater_N%C3%BCrnberg_2006-08-08.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Staatstheater_N%C3%BCrnberg_2006-08-08.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Nuremberg State Theatre</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bardentreffen_2013_3668.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Bardentreffen_2013_3668.jpg/220px-Bardentreffen_2013_3668.jpg" width="220" height="331" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Bardentreffen_2013_3668.jpg/330px-Bardentreffen_2013_3668.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Bardentreffen_2013_3668.jpg/440px-Bardentreffen_2013_3668.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="4288" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bardentreffen_2013_3668.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bardentreffen 2013</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Staatstheater_N%C3%BCrnberg" title="Staatstheater Nürnberg">Nuremberg State Theatre</a>, founded in 1906, is dedicated to all types of opera, ballet and stage theatre. During the season 2009/2010, the theatre presented 651 performances for an audience of 240,000 persons.<sup id="cite_ref-StaatsTheater_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StaatsTheater-16">[16]</a></sup> The State Philharmonic Nuremberg (<i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Staatsphilharmonie_N%C3%BCrnberg&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Staatsphilharmonie Nürnberg (page does not exist)">Staatsphilharmonie Nürnberg</a></i>) is the orchestra of the State Theatre. Its name was changed in 2011 from its previous name: The Nuremberg Philharmonic (<i>Nürnberger Philharmoniker</i>). It is the second-largest opera orchestra in Bavaria.<sup id="cite_ref-Philharmonic_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Philharmonic-17">[17]</a></sup> Besides opera performances, it also presents its own subscription concert series in the <i>Meistersingerhalle</i>. <a href="/wiki/Christof_Perick" title="Christof Perick">Christof Perick</a> was the principal conductor of the orchestra between 2006–2011. <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Bosch" title="Marcus Bosch">Marcus Bosch</a> heads the orchestra since September 2011 .</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Nuremberg Symphony Orchestra">Nuremberg Symphony Orchestra</a> (<i>Nürnberger Symphoniker</i>) performs around 100 concerts a year to a combined annual audience of more than 180,000.<sup id="cite_ref-Symphony_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Symphony-18">[18]</a></sup> The regular subscription concert series are mostly performed in the <i>Meistersingerhalle</i> but other venues are used as well, including the new concert hall of the <i>Kongresshalle</i> and the <i>Serenadenhof</i>. <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Shelley" title="Alexander Shelley">Alexander Shelley</a> has been the principal conductor of the orchestra since 2009.</p>
<p>The Nuremberg International Chamber Music Festival (<i>Internationales Kammermusikfestival Nürnberg</i>) takes place in early September each year, and in 2011 celebrated its tenth anniversary. Concerts take place around the city; opening and closing events are held in the medieval <i>Burg</i>. The <a href="/wiki/Bardentreffen" title="Bardentreffen">Bardentreffen</a>, an annual folk festival in Nuremberg, has been deemed the largest <a href="/wiki/World_music" title="World music">world music</a> festival in Germany and takes place since 1976. 2014 the Bardentreffen starred 368 artists from 31 nations.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:N%C3%BCrnberger_Bratw%C3%BCrste.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/N%C3%BCrnberger_Bratw%C3%BCrste.jpg/220px-N%C3%BCrnberger_Bratw%C3%BCrste.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/N%C3%BCrnberger_Bratw%C3%BCrste.jpg/330px-N%C3%BCrnberger_Bratw%C3%BCrste.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/N%C3%BCrnberger_Bratw%C3%BCrste.jpg/440px-N%C3%BCrnberger_Bratw%C3%BCrste.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:N%C3%BCrnberger_Bratw%C3%BCrste.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Nürnberger <a href="/wiki/Bratwurst" title="Bratwurst">Bratwurst</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Nuremberg is known for Nürnberger <a href="/wiki/Bratwurst" title="Bratwurst">Bratwurst</a> (grilled sausage), which is shorter and thinner than other bratwurst sausages.</p>
<p>Another Nuremberg speciality is Nürnberger <a href="/wiki/Lebkuchen" title="Lebkuchen">Lebkuchen</a>, a kind of ginger bread eaten mainly around Christmas time.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Germany_Nuernberg_Georg-Simon-Ohm-Fachhoschschule.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Germany_Nuernberg_Georg-Simon-Ohm-Fachhoschschule.jpg/190px-Germany_Nuernberg_Georg-Simon-Ohm-Fachhoschschule.jpg" width="190" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Germany_Nuernberg_Georg-Simon-Ohm-Fachhoschschule.jpg/285px-Germany_Nuernberg_Georg-Simon-Ohm-Fachhoschschule.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Germany_Nuernberg_Georg-Simon-Ohm-Fachhoschschule.jpg/380px-Germany_Nuernberg_Georg-Simon-Ohm-Fachhoschschule.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Germany_Nuernberg_Georg-Simon-Ohm-Fachhoschschule.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Technische_Hochschule_N%C3%BCrnberg" title="Technische Hochschule Nürnberg">Georg Simon Ohm</a> Technische Hochschule Nürnberg (Kesslerplatz).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Nuremberg offers 51 public and 6 private elementary schools in nearly all of its districts. Secondary education is offered at 23 <a href="/wiki/Mittelschule" title="Mittelschule">Mittelschulen</a>, 12 <a href="/wiki/Realschule" title="Realschule">Realschulen</a>, and 17 <a href="/wiki/Gymnasium_(Germany)" title="Gymnasium (Germany)">Gymnasien</a> (state, city, church, and privately owned). There are also several other providers of secondary education such as Berufsschule, Berufsfachschule, Wirtschaftsschule etc. <sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Higher_education">Higher education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Higher education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Nuremberg hosts the joint university <a href="/wiki/University_of_Erlangen-Nuremberg" title="University of Erlangen-Nuremberg">Friedrich-Alexander-Universität Erlangen-Nürnberg</a>, two Fachhochschulen (<a href="/wiki/Technische_Hochschule_N%C3%BCrnberg" title="Technische Hochschule Nürnberg">Technische Hochschule Nürnberg</a> and <i>Evangelische Hochschule Nürnberg</i>), an art school (<i>Akademie der Bildenden Künste Nürnberg</i>), and a music conservatoire <a href="/wiki/Hochschule_f%C3%BCr_Musik_N%C3%BCrnberg" title="Hochschule für Musik Nürnberg">(Hochschule für Musik Nürnberg</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> There are also private schools such as the <i>Akademie Deutsche POP Nürnberg</i> offering higher education.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_sights">Main sights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Main sights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:100%; max-width:1508px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nuremberg_from_Burg_17.04.2010.jpg" class="image" title="Nuremberg, seen from the castle"><img alt="A panoramic city view" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d5/Nuremberg_from_Burg_17.04.2010.jpg/1500px-Nuremberg_from_Burg_17.04.2010.jpg" width="1500" height="315" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d5/Nuremberg_from_Burg_17.04.2010.jpg/2250px-Nuremberg_from_Burg_17.04.2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d5/Nuremberg_from_Burg_17.04.2010.jpg/3000px-Nuremberg_from_Burg_17.04.2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6102" data-file-height="1281" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nuremberg_from_Burg_17.04.2010.jpg" title="File:Nuremberg from Burg 17.04.2010.jpg"></a></div>
Nuremberg, seen from the castle</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Castle" title="Nuremberg Castle">Nuremberg Castle</a>: the three castles that tower over the city including central burgraves' castle, with Free Reich's buildings to the east, the Imperial castle to the west.</li>
<li><i><a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heilig-Geist-Spital_(N%C3%BCrnberg)" class="extiw" title="de:Heilig-Geist-Spital (Nürnberg)">Heilig-Geist-Spital</a></i>. In the centre of the city, on the bank of the river Pegnitz, stands the Hospital of the Holy Spirit. Founded in 1332, this is one of the largest hospitals of the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>. Lepers were kept here at some distance from the other patients. It now houses elderly persons and a restaurant.</li>
<li>The <i>Hauptmarkt</i>, dominated by the front of the unique <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic</a> <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Frauenkirche" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuremberg Frauenkirche"><i>Frauenkirche</i></a> (Our Lady's Church), provides a picturesque setting for the famous <a href="/wiki/Christkindlesmarkt,_Nuremberg" title="Christkindlesmarkt, Nuremberg">Christmas market</a>. A main attraction on the square is the Gothic <i><a href="/wiki/Sch%C3%B6ner_Brunnen" title="Schöner Brunnen">Schöner Brunnen</a></i> (Beautiful Fountain) which was erected around 1385 but subsequently replaced with a replica (the original fountain is kept in the <a href="/wiki/Germanisches_Nationalmuseum" title="Germanisches Nationalmuseum">Germanisches Nationalmuseum</a>). The unchanged <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> bridge <i><a href="/wiki/Fleischbr%C3%BCcke" class="mw-redirect" title="Fleischbrücke">Fleischbrücke</a></i> crosses the Pegnitz nearby.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic</a> <a href="/wiki/St._Lorenz,_Nuremberg" title="St. Lorenz, Nuremberg"><i>Lorenzkirche</i></a> (St. Laurence church) dominates the southern part of the walled city and is one of the most important buildings in Nuremberg. The main body was built around 1270–1350.</li>
<li>The even earlier and equally impressive <a href="/wiki/St._Sebaldus_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Sebaldus Church"><i>Sebalduskirche</i></a> is St. Lorenz's counterpart in the northern part of the old city.</li>
<li>The church of the former <i><a href="/wiki/Katharinenkirche,_Nuremberg" title="Katharinenkirche, Nuremberg">Katharinenkloster</a></i> is preserved as a ruin, the <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Charterhouse" title="Nuremberg Charterhouse">charterhouse</a> (<i>Kartause</i>) is integrated into the building of the <a href="/wiki/Germanisches_Nationalmuseum" title="Germanisches Nationalmuseum">Germanisches Nationalmuseum</a> and the choir of the former <i>Franziskanerkirche</i> is part of a modern building.</li>
<li>Other churches located inside the city walls are: <a href="/wiki/St._Lorenz_(N%C3%BCrnberg)" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Lorenz (Nürnberg)">St. Laurence's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Clare_of_Assisi" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Clare of Assisi">Saint Clare's</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Martha,_Nuremberg" title="St. Martha, Nuremberg">Saint Martha's</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Jakob,_Nuremberg" title="St. Jakob, Nuremberg">Saint James the Greater's</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Egidien,_Nuremberg" title="St. Egidien, Nuremberg">Saint Giles's</a>, and <a href="/wiki/St._Elizabeth,_Nuremberg" title="St. Elizabeth, Nuremberg">Saint Elisabeth's</a>.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Germanisches_Nationalmuseum" title="Germanisches Nationalmuseum">Germanisches Nationalmuseum</a> is Germany's largest museum of cultural history, among its exhibits are works of famous painters such as Albrecht Dürer, <a href="/wiki/Rembrandt" title="Rembrandt">Rembrandt</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ernst_Ludwig_Kirchner" title="Ernst Ludwig Kirchner">Ernst Ludwig Kirchner</a>.</li>
<li>The Neues Museum Nürnberg is a museum for modern and contemporary art.</li>
<li>The Walburga Chapel and the Romanesque <i>Doppelkapelle</i> (Chapel with two floors) are part of Nuremberg Castle.</li>
<li>The <i>Johannisfriedhof</i> is a medieval cemetery, containing many old graves (Albrecht Dürer, <a href="/wiki/Willibald_Pirckheimer" title="Willibald Pirckheimer">Willibald Pirckheimer</a>, and others). The <i>Rochusfriedhof</i> or the Wöhrder Kirchhof are near the Old Town.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Chain_Bridge_(Nuremberg)" title="Chain Bridge (Nuremberg)">Chain Bridge</a> (<i>Kettensteg</i>), the first chain bridge on the European continent.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Tiergarten_N%C3%BCrnberg" class="mw-redirect" title="Tiergarten Nürnberg">Tiergarten Nürnberg</a> is a zoo stretching over more than 60 hectares (148 acres) in the <a href="/w/index.php?title=N%C3%BCrnberger_Reichswald&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nürnberger Reichswald (page does not exist)">Nürnberger Reichswald</a> forest.</li>
<li>There is also a medieval market just inside the city walls, selling handcrafted goods.</li>
<li>The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.dbmuseum.de">German National Railways Museum</a> <span class="languageicon">(in German)</span> (an Anchor Point of ERIH, The <a href="/wiki/European_Route_of_Industrial_Heritage" title="European Route of Industrial Heritage">European Route of Industrial Heritage</a>) is located in Nuremberg.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/File:Nuremberg_Ring.jpg" title="File:Nuremberg Ring.jpg">Nuremberg Ring</a> (now welded within an iron fence of Schöner Brunnen) is said to bring good luck to those that spin it.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Nazi_party_rally_grounds" title="Nazi party rally grounds">Nazi party rally grounds</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Documentation_Center_Nazi_Party_Rally_Grounds" title="Documentation Center Nazi Party Rally Grounds">documentation-center</a>.</li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The city's location next to numerous highways, railways, and a waterway has contributed to its rising importance for trade with Eastern Europe.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Railways">Railways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Railways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nuremberg.Central_railway_station.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Nuremberg.Central_railway_station.jpg/220px-Nuremberg.Central_railway_station.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Nuremberg.Central_railway_station.jpg/330px-Nuremberg.Central_railway_station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Nuremberg.Central_railway_station.jpg/440px-Nuremberg.Central_railway_station.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2056" data-file-height="1156" /></a>

<div class="thumb tright">

A subway station in Nuremberg.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/N%C3%BCrnberg_Hauptbahnhof" class="mw-redirect" title="Nürnberg Hauptbahnhof">Nürnberg Hauptbahnhof</a> is a stop for <a href="/wiki/InterCity" title="InterCity">IC</a> and <a href="/wiki/Intercity-Express" title="Intercity-Express">ICE</a> trains on the German long-distance railway network. The <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg%E2%80%93Munich_high-speed_railway" title="Nuremberg–Munich high-speed railway">Nuremberg–Ingolstadt–Munich high-speed line</a> with 300&#160;km/h (186&#160;mph) operation opened 28 May 2006, and was fully integrated into the rail schedule on 10 December 2006. Travel times to Munich have been reduced to as little as one hour. The <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg%E2%80%93Erfurt_high-speed_railway" title="Nuremberg–Erfurt high-speed railway">Nuremberg–Erfurt high-speed railway</a> is scheduled to open in December 2017.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="City_and_regional_transport">City and regional transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: City and regional transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DT3_Hauptbahnhof_TB.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/DT3_Hauptbahnhof_TB.JPG/220px-DT3_Hauptbahnhof_TB.JPG" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/DT3_Hauptbahnhof_TB.JPG/330px-DT3_Hauptbahnhof_TB.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/DT3_Hauptbahnhof_TB.JPG/440px-DT3_Hauptbahnhof_TB.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3165" data-file-height="1956" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DT3_Hauptbahnhof_TB.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An automatic <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_U-Bahn" title="Nuremberg U-Bahn">U-Bahn</a> train on the line <i><a href="/wiki/U3_(Nuremberg_U-Bahn)" title="U3 (Nuremberg U-Bahn)">U3</a></i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Trams_in_Nuremberg" title="Trams in Nuremberg">Nuremberg tramway network</a> was opened in 1881. As of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, it extended a total length of 36&#160;km (22&#160;mi), had six lines, and carried 39.152 million passengers annually. The first segment of the <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_U-Bahn" title="Nuremberg U-Bahn">Nuremberg U-Bahn</a> metro system was opened in 1972. Nuremberg's trams, <a href="/wiki/Bus" title="Bus">buses</a> and metro system are operated by the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://en.vag.de/">VAG Nürnberg</a> (<i>Verkehrsaktiengesellschaft Nürnberg</i> or Nuremberg Transport Corporation), itself a member of the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.vgn.de/?language=en">VGN</a> (<i>Verkehrsverbund Grossraum Nürnberg</i> or Greater Nuremberg Transport Network).</p>
<p>There is also a <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_S-Bahn" title="Nuremberg S-Bahn">Nuremberg S-Bahn</a> suburban metro railway and a regional train network, both centred on <a href="/wiki/N%C3%BCrnberg_Hauptbahnhof" class="mw-redirect" title="Nürnberg Hauptbahnhof">Nürnberg Hauptbahnhof</a>. Since 2008, Nuremberg has had the first U-Bahn in Germany (U2/U21 and U3) that works without a driver. It also was the first subway system worldwide in which both driver-operated trains and computer-controlled trains shared tracks.</p>
