<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Motorways">Motorways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Motorways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Nuremberg is conveniently located at the junction of several important Autobahn routes. The <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_3" title="Bundesautobahn 3">A3</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a></i>–<a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_am_Main" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt am Main">Frankfurt</a>–<a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrzburg" title="Würzburg">Würzburg</a>–<i><a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a></i>) passes in a south-easterly direction along the north-east of the city. The <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_9" title="Bundesautobahn 9">A9</a> (Berlin–Munich) passes in a north–south direction on the east of the city. The <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_6" title="Bundesautobahn 6">A6</a> (<i>France</i>–<a href="/wiki/Saarbr%C3%BCcken" title="Saarbrücken">Saarbrücken</a>–<i><a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a></i>) passes in an east–west direction to the south of the city. Finally, the <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_73" title="Bundesautobahn 73">A73</a> begins in the south-east of Nuremberg and travels north-west through the city before continuing towards Fürth and <a href="/wiki/Bamberg" title="Bamberg">Bamberg</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airport">Airport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Airport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Airport" title="Nuremberg Airport">Nuremberg Airport</a> has flights to major German cities and many European destinations, and is a <a href="/wiki/Focus_city" class="mw-redirect" title="Focus city">focus city</a> for <a href="/wiki/Air_Berlin" title="Air Berlin">Air Berlin</a>, Germany's second largest airline. A significant amount of the airport's traffic flies in and out during the peak winter season. The airport (Flughafen) is the terminus of subway line 2; it is the only airport in Germany served by a subway.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canals">Canals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Canals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Nuremberg is an important port on the <a href="/wiki/Rhine%E2%80%93Main%E2%80%93Danube_Canal" title="Rhine–Main–Danube Canal">Rhine–Main–Danube Canal</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankenstadion_3.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Frankenstadion_3.JPG/220px-Frankenstadion_3.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Frankenstadion_3.JPG/330px-Frankenstadion_3.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Frankenstadion_3.JPG/440px-Frankenstadion_3.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankenstadion_3.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Grundig-Stadion" class="mw-redirect" title="Grundig-Stadion">Grundig-Stadion</a> is the football stadium of <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> club <a href="/wiki/1._FC_Nuremberg" class="mw-redirect" title="1. FC Nuremberg">1. FC Nuremberg</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/1._FC_N%C3%BCrnberg" title="1. FC Nürnberg">1. FC Nürnberg</a>, known locally as <i>Der Club</i> (English: "The Club"), was founded in 1900 and plays in the <a href="/wiki/2._Bundesliga" title="2. Bundesliga">2. Bundesliga</a> (2016-2017 season). The official colours of the association are red and white, but the traditional colours are red and black. The current chairmen are Andreas Bornemann and Michael Meeske. They play in <a href="/wiki/Max-Morlock-Stadion" title="Max-Morlock-Stadion">Max-Morlock-Stadion</a> which was refurbished for the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 FIFA World Cup</a> and accommodates 50,000 spectators.</p>
<ul>
<li><b>German Champion:</b> 1920, 1921, 1924, 1925, 1927, 1936, 1948, 1961, 1968</li>
<li><b>German Cup:</b> 1935, 1939, 1962, 2007</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Basketball">Basketball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nuremberg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Basketball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <i>SELLBYTEL Baskets Nürnberg</i> played in the <a href="/wiki/Basketball_Bundesliga" title="Basketball Bundesliga">Basketball Bundesliga</a> from 2005 to 2007. Since then, teams from Nuremberg have attempted to return to Germany's elite league. The recently founded <a href="/wiki/N%C3%BCrnberg_Falcons_BC" title="Nürnberg Falcons BC">Nürnberg Falcons BC</a> have already established themselves as one of the main teams in Germany's second division <a href="/wiki/ProA" title="ProA">ProA</a> and aim to take on the heritage of the SELLBYTEL Baskets Nürnberg. The Falcons play their home games at the <i>Halle im Berufsbildungszentrum (BBZ)</i>.</p>
